# Liquid objects: content_for_header

[Skip to main content](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/liquid/objects/content_for_header#main-content)

Dynamically returns all scripts required by Shopify.

Include the `content_for_header` object in your [layout files](https://shopify.dev/themes/architecture/layouts)
 between the `<head>` and `</head>` HTML tags.

You shouldn't try to modify or parse the `content_for_header` object because the contents are subject to change, which can change the behaviour of your code.

* * *

Note

The `content_for_header` object is required in `theme.liquid`.

**Note:**

The `content_for_header` object is required in `theme.liquid`.

**Note:** The <code><span class="PreventFireFoxApplyingGapToWBR">content<wbr/>\_for<wbr/>\_header</span></code> object is required in <code>theme.liquid</code>.

* * *

### Directly accessible in

*   Global

# Liquid objects: page_description

# Reviews

[Skip to main content](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/app-home/apis/reviews#main-content)

Reviews


===========

Ask assistant

The Reviews API allows you to request an app review modal overlaid on your embedded app in the Shopify admin. You control when to request a modal, but it will only be displayed to the merchant if [certain conditions](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/app-home/apis/reviews#rate-limits-restrictions)
 are met.

[Anchor to reviews](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/app-home/apis/reviews#reviews)
Reviews


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The Reviews API provides a `request()` method that allows you to request an app review modal.

[Anchor to request](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/app-home/apis/reviews#reviews-propertydetail-request)

request**request**

() => Promise<ReviewRequestResponseReviewRequestResponse\>**() => Promise<ReviewRequestResponseReviewRequestResponse\>**

required**required**

### ReviewRequestResponse

    ReviewRequestSuccessResponse | ReviewRequestDeclinedResponse

### ReviewRequestSuccessResponse

*   code
    
        'success'
    
*   message
    
        'Review modal shown successfully'
    
*   success
    
        true
    

    export interface ReviewRequestSuccessResponse {
      success: true;
      code: 'success';
      message: 'Review modal shown successfully';
    }

### ReviewRequestDeclinedResponse

*   code
    
        ReviewRequestDeclinedCode
    
*   message
    
        string
    
*   success
    
        false
    

    export interface ReviewRequestDeclinedResponse {
      success: false;
      code: ReviewRequestDeclinedCode;
      message: string;
    }

### ReviewRequestDeclinedCode

    'mobile-app' | 'already-reviewed' | 'annual-limit-reached' | 'cooldown-period' | 'merchant-ineligible' | 'recently-installed' | 'already-open' | 'open-in-progress' | 'cancelled'

Examples

Request an app review modal

9

1

2

3

4

5

6

7

8

9

try {

const result \= await shopify.reviews.request();

if (!result.success) {

console.log(\`Review modal not displayed. Reason: ${result.code}: ${result.message}\`);

}

// if result.success \*is\* true, then review modal is displayed

} catch (error) {

console.error('Error requesting review:', error);

}

Preview
-------

![](https://cdn.shopify.com/shopifycloud/shopify-dev/production/assets/assets/images/templated-apis-screenshots/admin/apis/reviews-DTX8hadd.png)

### Examples

*   #### Request an app review modal
    
    ##### Default
    
        try {
          const result = await shopify.reviews.request();
          if (!result.success) {
            console.log(`Review modal not displayed. Reason: ${result.code}: ${result.message}`);
          }
          // if result.success *is* true, then review modal is displayed
        } catch (error) {
          console.error('Error requesting review:', error);
        }
        
    

[Anchor to responses](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/app-home/apis/reviews#responses)
Response codes and messages


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

A request to the Reviews API will return one of the following responses:

| success | code | message |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `true` | `success` | Review modal displayed |
| `false` | `mobile-app` | Review modal not supported on mobile devices |
| `false` | `already-reviewed` | Merchant already reviewed this app |
| `false` | `annual-limit-reached` | Review modal already displayed the maximum number of times within the last 365 days |
| `false` | `cooldown-period` | Review modal already displayed within the last 60 days |
| `false` | `merchant-ineligible` | Merchant isn't eligible to review this app |
| `false` | `recently-installed` | Merchant installed this app for less than 24 hours |
| `false` | `already-open` | Review modal is already open |
| `false` | `open-in-progress` | Review modal opening is already in progress |
| `false` | `cancelled` | Review modal opening was cancelled |

[Anchor to rate-limits-restrictions](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/app-home/apis/reviews#rate-limits-restrictions)
Rate limits and restrictions


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

A review modal will only be displayed to the merchant if certain conditions are met. Be sure to follow the [recommended best practices](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/app-home/apis/reviews#best-practices)
 for requesting reviews.

### Rate limits

The Reviews API applies rate limits to ensure a good merchant experience and to prevent abuse. A review modal will only be displayed to a merchant:

*   **Once** within any **60-day** period, and
*   **Three** times within any **365-day** period.

### Restrictions

A review modal will never be displayed in these cases:

*   The merchant already reviewed your app.
*   The merchant is on a mobile device.
*   The merchant is ineligible to leave a review.
*   The merchant has installed your app for less than 24 hours

[Anchor to best-practices](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/app-home/apis/reviews#best-practices)
Best practices for review requests


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Because you can make only a [limited number](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/app-home/apis/reviews#rate-limits-restrictions)
 of requests for review, make sure to choose the right time:

*   **Do** request a review at the end of a successful workflow.
*   **Don't** request a review at any point that interrupts a merchant task.
*   **Don't** request a review as soon as the merchant opens your app.
*   **Don't** trigger a request with a button, link, or other call to action. Because the request might be rate-limited and the modal isn't guaranteed to display, your app UI would appear to be broken.

[Anchor to testing-the-reviews-api](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/app-home/apis/reviews#testing-the-reviews-api)
Testing the Reviews API


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can use your development store to test the Reviews API, which bypasses the rate limits and restrictions. Reviews submitted from development stores are not published on the Shopify App Store.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

# Liquid tags: javascript

[Skip to main content](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/liquid/tags/javascript#main-content)

JavaScript code included in [section](https://shopify.dev/storefronts/themes/architecture/sections)
, [block](https://shopify.dev/storefronts/themes/architecture/blocks)
 and [snippet](https://shopify.dev/storefronts/themes/architecture/snippets)
 files.

Each section, block or snippet can have only one `{% javascript %}` tag.

To learn more about how JavaScript that's defined between the `javascript` tags is loaded and run, refer to the documentation for [javascript tags](https://shopify.dev/storefronts/themes/best-practices/javascript-and-stylesheet-tags#javascript)
.

* * *

Caution

Liquid isn't rendered inside of `{% javascript %}` tags. Including Liquid code can cause syntax errors.

**Caution:**

Liquid isn't rendered inside of `{% javascript %}` tags. Including Liquid code can cause syntax errors.

**Caution:** Liquid isn&#39;t rendered inside of <code>{% javascript %}</code> tags. Including Liquid code can cause syntax errors.

* * *

Syntax
------

9

1

2

3

{% javascript %}

javascript\_code

{% endjavascript %}

javascript\_code

The JavaScript code for the section, block or snippet.

# Future flags

[Skip to main content](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/shopify-app-react-router/latest/guide-future-flags#main-content)

Future flags
============

Similarly to how [React Router approaches breaking changes](https://reactrouter.com/6.30.0/guides/api-development-strategy#future-flags)
, the `@shopify/shopify-app-react-router` package also uses future flags.

Bigger features and breaking changes are initially added behind a future flag. This means that they're disabled by default, and must be manually enabled by setting the appropriate flag in the `future` option of the `shopifyApp` function.

This allows apps to gradually adopt new features, and prepare for breaking changes and major releases ahead of time.

Ask assistant

* * *

Choose a version:

v1 latestv0

v1latest

[Anchor to Setting future flags](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/shopify-app-react-router/latest/guide-future-flags#setting-future-flags)
Setting future flags


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To opt in to a feature, simply enable the appropriate flag in the `future` option of the `shopifyApp` function.

Once a flag is set, the returned `shopify` object will start using the new APIs, including using any new types. That allows apps to rely on TypeScript to use a feature regardless of a flag being enabled or not.

* * *

[Anchor to Unstable APIs](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/shopify-app-react-router/latest/guide-future-flags#unstable-apis)
Unstable APIs


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When introducing new features to the package for which we want to gather feedback, we will add them behind a future flag, starting with the `unstable_` prefix.

That allows early adopters to try them out individually, without having to install a release candidate package.

When the feature is ready for release, the future flag will be removed and it will be available by default.

In this example, `shopify` has a new function called `newFeature`. If the future flag is disabled, TypeScript will be unaware of the new function, and the app will fail to compile if it tries to use it.

* * *

[Anchor to Breaking changes](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/shopify-app-react-router/latest/guide-future-flags#breaking-changes)
Breaking changes


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Similarly to unstable APIs, breaking changes will be introduced behind a future flag.

This allows apps to prepare for the next major version ahead of time, and to gradually adopt the new APIs.

When the next major version is released, the future flag will be removed, and the old code it changes will be removed. Apps that adopted the flag before then will continue to work the same way with no new changes.

* * *

[Anchor to Supported flags](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/shopify-app-react-router/latest/guide-future-flags#supported-flags)
Supported flags


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

There are currently no future flags in the current version.

* * *

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

# Subscription apps

[Skip to main content](https://shopify.dev/docs/apps/design/user-experience/subscription-apps#main-content)

Subscription apps
=================

Subscription apps offer customers a subscription purchase option. To ensure a positive experience for customers, subscription apps should follow these design guidelines.

### Guidance

This guide explains the key principles of subscription needs and component-level guidelines for implementing subscription user interfaces. Refer to the [subscriptions section](https://shopify.dev/docs/storefronts/themes/pricing-payments/subscriptions/subscription-ux-guidelines)
 of Shopify.dev for more details.

![Subscription information that matches the storefront theme.](https://cdn.shopify.com/shopifycloud/shopify-dev/production/assets/assets/images/app-design-guidelines/subscription-apps/clear-price-DObOTNYr.png)

The price of a subscription should be clearly visible when a customer has selected a selling plan from a product form.

![Subscription information that matches the storefront theme.](https://cdn.shopify.com/shopifycloud/shopify-dev/production/assets/assets/images/app-design-guidelines/subscription-apps/match-styles-CGhGU4kH.png)

Subscription related UI should match the color palette, font, font-size and font weight of the store's current theme by default.

[![Forms](https://cdn.shopify.com/shopifycloud/shopify-dev/production/assets/assets/images/spot-icons/adg-forms-wmPS0Hm4.png)![Forms](https://cdn.shopify.com/shopifycloud/shopify-dev/production/assets/assets/images/spot-icons/adg-forms-wmPS0Hm4.png)\
\

\

\-Forms](https://shopify.dev/docs/apps/design/user-experience/forms)

[\#### Previous - Forms](https://shopify.dev/docs/apps/design/user-experience/forms)

.

The `payment_terms` filter must be used on the `form` object within a [product form](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/liquid/tags/form#form-product)
 or [cart form](https://shopify.dev/docs/api/liquid/tags/form#form-cart)
.
